I had visit this place on December/27/2020.
Spoony me.....I was looking for the garden with a lot of flowers but after about 1.5 miles hiking in, and I found out....
The name Garden of Eden is a misnomer.
There is no garden but a beautiful forest and scenery river flowing through it.
It was a bit confusing because no sign board or gate.
It is a small pool and boulders, very awesome spot if you love water holes.
The hike along the train tracks is lovely and a lot of fun. 99 percent of the trail is shaded,super easy, and not many people.
Wish I had gone when it was warmer to enjoy swimming!
It‚Äôs totally worth the effort.<//Review>

If you're expecting a calm and serene vista (like the name "garden of eden" would suggest), then this is probably not it. What this actually is is a pretty crowded swimming hole, usually filled with music, alcohol, and weed. This isn't necessarily a bad thing if that's what you want, but just be prepared a fairly crowded teen hangout. The walk there involves some steep hills and some walking along the train tracks to get to the only real place you can get down to the river<//review>

< Text>
The San Lorenzo river is very dirty. Trash is everywhere. Crowded all day everyday from march to november. Every year people disregard the rules and get too drunk or dive off the rocks and have to get airlifted out of the valley. Stick to the beaches east of cowells that are more sheltered from the wind (sunny cove, etc.) if you want a nice summertime spot to jump in the water.<//Text>

1570665384059<//date>
< rate>
4<//rate>
<Text>The name Garden of Eden is a misnomer, and you are in for a surprise. There is no garden but a beautiful forest with a calm river flowing through it.

We had a bit of confusion with the entrance as we drioe through redwoods. There is no gate or any sign board, but there is an area where you can park the car. We assumed that is the entrance and thought of checking it out. There is no other sign even when you enter and no info about the trail. We kept on walking with an assumption that it will lead to the river. And it did.! We go through the hill in a winding downhill trail to reach near the river. The trail continues parallel to the river and there are a few spots that you can access the river.

We went around 4-5 pm, and it gets pretty dark due to the tree cover. There were some families spending time with the kids, and enjoying bathing in the river.

We spent only less than an hour, and am sure there was more to hike and see. Since there was no other information about the trail, am not sure how long it is. We returned after we spent some time in the river. The uphill hike was a lot more tiring, but it was worth.< /Text><pictures>None</pictures><Response>None</Response>< gmapID>
0x808e4139244fc2a3:0x8a6b23de7218b575<//gmapID>

< review>
A nice spot to go for a swim. It's close to a lot of good hiking trails and the distinctive old railroad bridge. The biggest downside (as others have pointed out) is that it can get very crowded and many of the people who go are disrespectful to the natural beauty of the place, so if you go PLEASE pick up after yourself.

While this isn't my favorite place on the San Lorenzo, it's worth going to.<//review>

<Rating>5</Rating><Text>I'm a volunteer for the park, and for the past 12 years I've taken on the task of keeping the Garden of Eden a Garden. And let me tell you, it's a full time job, especially on summer weekends, when hundreds of people come to enjoy it. So here's the deal: no dogs, no fires, no alcohol, leave no trash, out by sunset. And if you think it's okay to ignore the rules, you are likely to run into a park ranger ready to write you a ticket--minimum $300 fine. Please, please come and enjoy the Garden, but it's not a party spot. It's a place for peaceful reflection and reverence of the beauty we find in the natural world.
So many dogs! Even if you pick up after your dog, their paws on dirt leave a scent that scares local wildlife. Please come and visit the Garden, but please don't bring your dog. Instead, walk the paved Pipeline Road for 4 miles, where dogs are allowed. And no dogs ever in the river.<//Text><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< Response>

<date>1498668442882<//date><Rate>1<//Rate>< Review>
Unfortunately, due to the high volume of visitors the beauty of the Garden of Eden is the same as it once was.

When going to any public park, it should be common sense to not disregard signs that tell you "no alcoholic beverages are permitted beyond this point." Or "pick up your trash." Instead, that's what has happened at the Garden of Eden over the past few years. Last year, someone died here.

If you do go, please do your part to preserve - pack out all trash, including your feces.</Review>

<Rate>5< /Rate>< Text>
I had a delightful experience at this new store. The store is clean. And, the customer service is outstanding. For example, I asked an employee where is the bread. She stopped what she was doing and took us to the bread aisle. There are some innovations to the grocery shopping experience too. They have technology-enhanced shopping carts they call dash carts. It totals up what you put in the cart as you shop. It's like self-service check out on steroids. I love the way Amazon has placed a cashier display facing the consumer. It's easier to see and stay on budget. I love the fact that they have biodegradable paper shopping bags. The thing I love most about this shopping experience is the fact that all the employees have good morale, are friendly, and accurately reflect the ethnic diversity of the neighborhood. Everyone I asked if they like working there said, Yes!< /Text>

< text>
We are not from the area so it was our first time visiting an Amazon store.  We tried out the "Dash" cart, the one that gets tied to your Amazon account and automatically tracks/charges you for what you put in the cart.

The staff gave us a tutorial of how to use it, and it was quick and easy. The cart functioned flawlessly and checkout was a breeze.

Prices at this location seemed really high, not sure if that's an LA thing or an "Amazon Fresh" thing but a pack of gum and 2 cucumbers ran us $9.65 which seemed awfully high.

Anyway, we came here for the experience and were not dissapointed!</text>

< Review>
This Amazon fresh is newly opened. The shopping experience was great. I used the new carts that scan items as you out them in the cart. It was fast and easy and if items scanned twice it was an easy fix. The interface on the screen is easy to understand and check out was easy. If you need more bags you grab them and your amazon primary card is automatically charged. The only reason I gave it a 4 star instead of a 5 is due to the prices. I do quite alot of shopping and some of their items are cheaper at other stores. All in all a good experience but I will probably only shop here when I'm looking for better quality specific items I can't find at my local grocery store.< /Review>

< Review>
One of the best Kaiser. Staff are friendly here and treat you like a human being. Their volunteer staff are always willing to point you in the right direction, and help you push the wheelchair.

Their pharmacy can be a zoo and the wait can be challenging. The line to drop off your prescription is pretty quick, but on a normal day, you can expect anywhere between 15 to 30 minute wait and then have to wait in line for another 15 minutes to pick up the prescription and if you have a consultation that can add another 10 minutes.

The parking lot can get pretty full by mid day but you can always find an open space.

They also have a pretty nice cafeteria with decent food. You would think a place like this would have mediocre food because you have no choice, but it's actually not bad. They have a variety of healthy choices at reasonable priced. I paid $5.99 for a chicken taco salad. Cafeteria dining area is pretty big so there's ample seating. They even have a public microwave to warm up your own lunch too</Review>

<Date>1529880197097< /Date>< Review>
This restaurant was an amazing find and is a must visit for lovers of Salvadorian food. Having lived in El Salvador for two years I can promise that the pupusas served there are legit and also boast loroco as an option, a condiment not every restaurant has. The atmosphere here is also very friendly with authentic loud music and kind waiters. If I had the opportunity I would be a regular here, but the least I can do is write this glowing review for anyone deciding if they should eat here. 5 stars!<//Review>

<rating>5< /rating>< Text>
Having lived in El Salvador for two years, I can testify to the authenticity of this place. I could tell as we walked in and heard the music playing louder than the typical American joint that this place is authentic. We ordered horchata and pupusas and they did not dissapoint. The Salvadorian horchata is the most authentic I've had since being back in the states and the pupusas are amazing without being too costly. Another way I could tell this restaurant is authentic is that the server began talking to us in Spanish (even though we don't necessarily look like we speak it). Don't let this discourage you though if you haven't brushed up on your espa√±ol since our waiter switched to English when we didn't understand everything.< /Text>

< Review>
Overall our dinner was very good! The veggies were fresh and tasty, and the hummus and baba ganouj were awesome. The falafel patties blew me away! We liked the beet delite, but both found the grape leaves to be just ok. I loved the tabbouleh, but my wife wasn‚Äôt a fan.

The vegetarian tacos were pretty good - the black bean chili had a great flavor, but the steamed veggies, and the brown rice on the side, were pretty bland. The side salad was good. The overlapping tacos was strange - the pitas were overlapping each other and filled together, so to eat them you had to pull them apart and spread the filling from one to the empty space in the other.

The outdoor seating area was nice, but there was a fair amount of road noise until rush hour died down - nothing they can do about that, though.<//Review>

< Text>
Awesome, healthy, vegetarian food. I was so sad when they stopped serving their teriyaki salmon! It used to come with grilled veggies, a salad, brown rice, and sooooooooo much of that good teriyaki sauce! PLEASE add this to your menu again, my family loves it and I want other people to get to enjoy it too!
The rest of the food here is equally good (once my family finished mourning their favorite dish, they instantly found a new group of favorites...aka the whole menu). The vegetarian/vegan options are totally great! I haven't eaten meat in so long that I don't remember what a burger tastes like, but even over all that time I just haven't been able to make a meal of some of the overly-healthy vegan food that some places serve. I mean, I just don't feel full unless I have a protein, you know? So I was super happy when my family found this place, because they had super good falafels (which are really filling), a lot of their non-mean dishes incorporate beans and other protein-packed legumes, and overall their vegetarian dishes are super comforting while still being healthy and ethical! The omnivores in my family always talk loudly about how good the meat dishes are, so this place is perfect for everyone!
Oh, not to mention they serve KILLER breakfasts!</Text>

Food, meh. Service, not good.

Ordered the spinach quesadilla, which the menu says to allow an extra 10 minutes for.  Apparantly this message didnt get to the wait staff because our entree arrived about 3 minutes after the app.  (At least this explains the unwillingness of our waitress to change my wife's order 3 minutes after we put it in - we thought that with an extra 10 minutes it wouldnt be an issue... it was).

I ordered the chicken shwarma which was a gluey purple mess with about 5 pieces of chicken in it.  Not nearly enough of the thin, dry, burnt pita to eat it with.  Overall a poor presentation for a weak dish.

My wife had the veggie kebab (she tried to change out for a veggie burger which we didnt see on the front of the menu initially,  but this could not be accommodated. Even just a few minutes after ordering and well before our app).  It was ok.  It says there is pineapple in it, and the tiny piece we found between everything else makes it true (but hardly worth a mention in the menu).  1 kebab, a ton of flavorless,  mushy brown rice, and mediocre hummus and mushy  sides.  Overall, not great.

We had high hopes.  Disappointed.<//Text>
